#### Define sets of values
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Many datasets contain items that are distinct, but related.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=5)** For example, you might have states or sales regions from the same part of the country that you would like to combine.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=12)** In this movie, I will show you how to do that by defining a set.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=17)** My sample file is 0905 sets, and you can find it in the chapter nine folder of the exercise files collection.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=25)** I'm demonstrating how to create sets using the data model, but it works for other pivot tables as well.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=32)** In the pivot table, in the row labels area, I have sales regions and I might want to create a set that will contain every region that has central in the name, so Central East, North Central East, North Central West, South Central East, and South Central West.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=53)** To create that set, I can go to the pivot table, analyze contextual tab, assuming that a cell within the pivot table has been selected.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=62)** And then in the calculations group, I'll click Fields, Items & Sets.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=68)** And at the bottom, I'll click Create Set Based on Row Items.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=74)** I could also do it for columns, but I'll use row because I have a clear idea of what I want.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=79)** So I'll click there and the new set dialogue box appears.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=85)** I will delete the existing name and I'll call it central regions.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=91)** And now I can choose which fields to eliminate and which to include.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=96)** So the first three all have Central in their name, so I will keep them.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=101)** I'll click next to Northeast and click Delete.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=105)** Northwest the same, these two, I'll keep.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=108)** Southeast, I'll delete, Southwest, I'll delete and all I will delete.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=114)** And again, these are only for use within the set.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=118)** I'm not actually deleting those fields or those values from the overall data set.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=124)** I'll leave everything else the same and click OK.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=129)** And over in the pivot table Fields task pane under customer's table, if I scroll down below the fields, I see that I now have a set called Central Regions, and also it has been applied to the pivot table.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=145)** If I clear the central regions checkbox or drag central regions from the Rose area off, then I don't have anything in the rows area, but if I drag sales region down, then I get my rows.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=162)** And if I drag central regions back down below sales region, I get an error saying that a set cannot be added at the same time as a field on which is based.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=174)** and that makes sense, so I'll click OK.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=178)** And central Regions replaced the sales region field as a whole.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=185)** Sets are a great way of combining related data without having to create a new field within a pivot table.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/excel-pivottables-in-depth-23781270/define-sets-of-values?u=76281980&t=192)** I encourage you to play around with them because I think they will add a lot of power to your data analysis.
